<tr>
<td style="line-height:normal;padding:6px 5px 3px;text-align:center"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar"><span style="word-spacing:0">This diagram: </span><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:SunRail_RDT" title="Template:SunRail RDT"><span title="View this template">view</span></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:SunRail_RDT" title="Template talk:SunRail RDT"><span title="Discuss this template">talk</span></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:SunRail_RDT&amp;action=edit"><span title="Edit this template">edit</span></a></li></ul></div>

<p><b>SunRail</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail" title="Commuter rail">commuter rail</a> system in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Orlando" title="Greater Orlando">Greater Orlando</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>, area.  Service began on May 1, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-StartOfServiceMay2014_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StartOfServiceMay2014-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>  The system comprises 16 stations<sup id="cite_ref-StartOfServiceMay2014_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StartOfServiceMay2014-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> along a former <a href="/wiki/CSX_Transportation" title="CSX Transportation">CSX Transportation</a> line connecting <a href="/wiki/Volusia_County" class="mw-redirect" title="Volusia County">Volusia County</a> and <a href="/wiki/Osceola_County,_Florida" title="Osceola County, Florida">Osceola County</a> through <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Orlando" title="Downtown Orlando">Downtown Orlando</a>.  The SunRail system is financed by the state and federal governments and the counties it serves. SunRail is Florida's second commuter rail system after <a href="/wiki/South_Florida" title="South Florida">South Florida</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Tri-Rail" title="Tri-Rail">Tri-Rail</a>.
</p><p>In the first quarter of 2019, the system averaged 6,362 paying riders per weekday.<sup id="cite_ref-cfcrc_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfcrc-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> A southern extension to Poinciana via Kissimmee, with four additional stations, opened on July 30, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Phase2Open_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Phase2Open-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/South_Florida_Railroad" title="South Florida Railroad">South Florida Railroad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Tampa_and_Key_West_Railway" title="Jacksonville, Tampa and Key West Railway">Jacksonville, Tampa and Key West Railway</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cost_and_funding">Cost and funding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cost and funding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The total cost of the system was originally estimated at $615 million for construction plus $432 million to purchase the right of way and tracks. However, the cost of construction ended up being above the $615 million quoted, and the agreement still allows CSX to run a limited number of freight trains along the line at night, although the majority of the freight traffic has been rerouted west to CSX's "S" Line.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The budgeted operating costs are $47 million, and the rider fare revenue is $2,210,000, resulting in an operating deficit of approximately $45 million, or over $50 per passenger.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Volusia_County,_Florida" title="Volusia County, Florida">Volusia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seminole_County,_Florida" title="Seminole County, Florida">Seminole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_Florida" title="Orange County, Florida">Orange</a> and <a href="/wiki/Osceola_County,_Florida" title="Osceola County, Florida">Osceola</a> counties and the <a href="/wiki/Orlando" class="mw-redirect" title="Orlando">City of Orlando</a> partnered to build the project. The project was financed by the federal government, the state of Florida, and the local partners. Fifty percent of the funding came from a federal transit "New Starts" grant. The local partners were responsible for 25 percent of the cost and another 25 percent was paid by the State of Florida, which included the cost of track improvements, construction of train stations, and purchasing of locomotives and rail cars.
</p><p>On 22 December 2010, it was announced that the state of Florida had created an <a href="/wiki/Escrow_account" class="mw-redirect" title="Escrow account">escrow account</a> with <a href="/wiki/US_dollar" class="mw-redirect" title="US dollar">$</a>173 million.<sup id="cite_ref-22dec_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22dec-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The money was planned to be used to purchase the tracks SunRail operates on, and also allowed the state to formally request $300 million from the federal government to cover construction costs.<sup id="cite_ref-22dec_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22dec-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During its first year of operation, SunRail made a total of $7.2 million from a combination of fares, advertising and fees paid by CSX and Amtrak to run their trains through the corridor.  However, SunRail spent a total of $34.4 million during that same year, ending it with a $27.2 million deficit and an average daily ridership of 3,700 passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Project_planning_and_approvals">Project planning and approvals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Project planning and approvals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At the end of July 2007, <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_Florida" title="Orange County, Florida">Orange County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seminole_County,_Florida" title="Seminole County, Florida">Seminole County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Osceola_County,_Florida" title="Osceola County, Florida">Osceola County</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volusia_County,_Florida" title="Volusia County, Florida">Volusia County</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">city of Orlando</a> all voted on and approved the Sunrail project.  Osceola County had agreed in principle, but was still examining how to fund its $9.3-million share at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-orlandosentinel1_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orlandosentinel1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-orlandosentinel1_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orlandosentinel1-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>An agreement was reached between Florida Department of Transportation and CSX for the purchase of the tracks on November 29, 2007, and the Florida Legislature approved the CSX-Florida Department of Transportation agreement in order for project construction to begin. However, the legislature failed to vote on the agreement to purchase the right of way and tracks from CSX in the 2008 session. At issue were provisions regarding liability and indemnification. Commenting on the bill, state senator <a href="/wiki/Paula_Dockery" title="Paula Dockery">Paula Dockery</a> said, "I don't envision a time anytime soon where thoughtful senators are going to say that there's some kind of good public policy involved in taking liability away from somebody who was at fault and putting it on the taxpayers of the state of Florida."<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The contract between CSX and Florida DOT was in place through June 30, 2009, and the legislature planned to use another opportunity to consider and approve the agreement in the 2009 legislative session.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The bill made it through all necessary Senate committee approvals and the first segment of the project had already been approved to enter Final Design by the Federal Transit Administration on August 11, 2008.
</p><p>On January 14, 2009, the SunRail name and logo were presented to the public by Orlando Mayor <a href="/wiki/Buddy_Dyer" title="Buddy Dyer">Buddy Dyer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Progress continued to move slowly forward on the project until the state legislative session on April 30, 2009, when the project was once again defeated by a 23-17 vote. The movement against the project, which was once again led by state senators Paula Dockery and Mike, continued to revolve around an amendment that would have approved a $200 million insurance policy for SunRail.   Another political problem for SunRail was an overall lack of support for the project from the South Florida delegation (which included state senators Chris Smith of Fort Lauderdale, Dan Gelber of Miami Beach, Nan Rich of Weston and Frederica Wilson of Miami) effectively killed the bill.
</p><p>After the second failure, with the deadline to purchase the tracks in question from CSX looming, the state initially pulled the plan from the legislative agenda, endangering as much as $307 million in federal funds that had been promised to SunRail, which would have been taken away if the plan failed. Nearly $27 million of that federal money had already been spent to purchase rail equipment and land for stations and it was unknown whether or not the state of Florida would have had to pay the money back to the federal government. However, CSX rescinded the deadline on June 29,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> permitting more negotiation time for insurance arrangements. An agreement on insurance was finally reached, and lawmakers convened a special session in December 2009 that passed the House on December 7 and the Senate on December 8. Additional federal money may be attracted to reduce the financial cost to the state.<sup id="cite_ref-orlandosentinel.com_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orlandosentinel.com-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 8, 2009, the contractual requirement necessary to move forward with SunRail was passed along with funding for South Florida's <a href="/wiki/Tri-Rail" title="Tri-Rail">Tri-Rail</a> system. At the bill's signing Senate President Jeff Atwater said "Today, Florida is embracing the opportunity to lead the nation in developing a comprehensive transportation system, thereby ensuring our competitive edge in the 21st Century global economy. A comprehensive transportation system, creating opportunities and avenues to connect employers and employees, is integral to building a stronger future for Florida."<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Negotiations with Amtrak subsequently led to a dispute over which party would bear liability for incidents on Amtrak trains operating on the route, which would be owned by SunRail&#8212;Amtrak wanted SunRail to assume responsibility for such incidents, while SunRail wanted Amtrak to be liable. The purchase of the trackage from CSX could not be completed until an agreement with Amtrak was reached.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> On December 10, 2010, it was announced that Amtrak and the state had apparently reached a deal regarding the issue, as Amtrak had dropped its opposition to the sale.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 29, 2011, Florida Governor <a href="/wiki/Rick_Scott" title="Rick Scott">Rick Scott</a> froze all SunRail contracts and ordered a six-month legislative review of the project to determine whether the project was a good investment.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>  However, on July 1, 2011, <a href="/wiki/Florida_Department_of_Transportation" title="Florida Department of Transportation">Florida Department of Transportation</a> Secretary Ananth Prasad announced that Scott had finally approved the project.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Phase 1 construction contract was awarded to two primary general contractors; RailWorks Track Systems, Inc. of New York City, who would be responsible for right-of-way and track improvements, and Atlanta-based Archer Western Contractors Ltd., who would be responsible for building the stations.<sup id="cite_ref-SunRail_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SunRail-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Work would include <a href="/wiki/Double_track" class="mw-redirect" title="Double track">double tracking</a> the existing line; the installation of new wayside signals; improvements to existing grade crossings; construction of the station platforms, canopies and adjacent parking areas; as well as building of the Operations Control Center and Vehicle Storage &amp; Maintenance Facility at CSX's Rand Yard in <a href="/wiki/Sanford,_Florida" title="Sanford, Florida">Sanford</a>.
</p><p>Ground was broken at the future Altamonte Springs station site on January 27, 2012, marking the official beginning of construction for Phase 1 of the SunRail project.<sup id="cite_ref-RTS_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RTS-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The first load of steel rail for double tracking the route between Sanford and <a href="/wiki/Longwood,_Florida" title="Longwood, Florida">Longwood</a> was delivered not long after in early 2012.  A second set of rails for double tracking the route between North Street in Longwood and Gore Street south of Downtown Orlando was delivered at the end of March 2012, and a third set, which supplemented various locations between Sanford and Orlando, was delivered at the end of July 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-orlandosentinel_03-22-12_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orlandosentinel_03-22-12-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thirdset_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thirdset-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The sections of standard <a href="/wiki/Rail_profile#North_America" title="Rail profile">115-pounds-per-yard</a> rail were 1650 feet long, weighing 31 tons each.<sup id="cite_ref-thirdset_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thirdset-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> On September 28, 2012, the St. Johns River <a href="/wiki/Bascule_bridge" title="Bascule bridge">drawbridge</a> in Sanford was closed for 54 hours while construction crews demolished and replaced the bridge approach spans.<sup id="cite_ref-orlandosentinel_09-26-12_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-orlandosentinel_09-26-12-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> By the time Phase 1 construction was completed in early 2014, nearly 32 miles of main line single track were double-tracked, three existing CSX freight yards were reconfigured, wayside signal and grade crossing signal improvements were made along the corridor, a total of 12 stations were built, and a new Operations Control Center and Vehicle Storage &amp; Maintenance Facility were constructed.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operational_history">Operational history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Operational history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>SunRail curtailed late night train service on 21st December 2015 citing ridership. A mid-day train to service leisure riders was introduced.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>SunRail has tested a few Saturday train operations. The test was from November 2016 to January 2017 but it did not happen every Saturday. Train service has been run on a Saturday after the supposed end date of January with the latest being on March 18th. This day set a ridership record with 12,842 passengers and is attributed to several events running in Orlando, specifically the Winter Park Sidewalk Arts Festival and an Orlando City Soccer Club soccer match. This headcount far outpaces the daily weekday ridership record of 8,842.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Several major businesses including the Downtown Orlando Partnership and Downtown Development Board are donating funds to pay for Saturday service. It's estimated the cost is $20,000+ each Saturday. Each company involved gives money towards the operating expenses in exchange for on-train advertising, logo placement on stations and billboards, and social media promotions. <sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Weekend trains will run between afternoon and evenings and are adjusted to serve specific events. The cost of running trains on Saturday is about $20,000. <sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> This service was to start in November 5th.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Phase_2_South">Phase 2 South</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Phase 2 South">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This segment extended the system 17 miles south from Sand Lake Road into Osceola County with a stop at the existing <a href="/wiki/Kissimmee_(Amtrak_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kissimmee (Amtrak station)">Kissimmee Amtrak station</a> as well as new stations being built in <a href="/wiki/Meadow_Woods,_Florida" title="Meadow Woods, Florida">Meadow Woods</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hunter%27s_Creek,_Florida" title="Hunter&#39;s Creek, Florida">Hunter's Creek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poinciana_(SunRail_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="Poinciana (SunRail station)">Poinciana</a>. Because federal funding in the amount of $93 million<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> was secured for <i>Phase 2 South</i>, construction on this segment began first.  
</p><p>On August 14, 2015, the state of Florida received the full funding grant agreement from the Federal Transit Administration that moved forward completion of SunRail <i>Phase 2 South</i>. Congressman <a href="/wiki/John_Mica" title="John Mica">John Mica</a> stated that because of the expedited agreement, full funding for the additional 17-mile extension was expected to be approved by the end of September.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> On September 28, 2015, the $93 million grant was formally approved at a ceremony at the Kissimmee Amtrak station.<sup id="cite_ref-sept_2015_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sept_2015-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> With matching state and local funding already in place providing an additional $93 million, construction on <i>Phase 2 South</i> was expected to begin in December 2015, but the Florida Department of Transportation delayed the selection of a design/build team until October 26, 2015, thus pushing back the start date by approximately a month.<sup id="cite_ref-bizjournals.com_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bizjournals.com-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite the delay in starting construction on <i>Phase 2 South</i>, the city of Kissimmee broke ground at the end of October 2015 on a parking structure next to the proposed Kissimmee SunRail Station and existing Multimodal Center, which is used by the Lynx and <a href="/wiki/Greyhound_Lines" title="Greyhound Lines">Greyhound</a> bus services. The parking structure was officially opened on May 10, 2017, and is four stories tall, accommodates 398 cars, and offers EV charging stations and LED lighting that dims when the garage is empty. The cost was $9 million.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> It was also announced that <a href="/wiki/Tupperware_Brands" title="Tupperware Brands">Tupperware Brands Corporation</a> added an extra $120,000 for upgrades to the Hunter's Creek Station, which will be built on land near their headquarters. This was done in exchange for naming rights to the station, which is now called the Tupperware Station. This funding will be used for additional landscaping and lighting along with cosmetic upgrades to the station design so that it will mimic the Tupperware headquarters building.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Congressman John Mica announced on November 25, 2015, that $63 million in federal dollars were on the way to assist the completion of <i>Phase 2 South</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> On March 28, 2016, the Florida Department of Transportation gave notice that <i>Phase 2 South</i> construction would begin on April 1, 2016, with service expected to begin by February 2018. A construction commencement ceremony took place on April 25, 2016, at 10:00 AM at the site of the future Tupperware Station, which officially kicked off construction.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Dana B. Kenyon Company of Jacksonville, Florida was awarded the $31.7 million contract for the Phase 2 southern extension project, including construction at each of the four new stations andnew vehicle storage and maintenance facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Train testing on the southern extension began in February 2018<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> and revenue service was inaugurated on July 30.<sup id="cite_ref-Phase2Open_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Phase2Open-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Service">Service</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Service">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schedule">Schedule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Schedule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>SunRail runs on weekdays excluding holidays in the daytime and on weekends if a sponsor pays to keep the service open, for instance sports or festival organisers.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> SunRail says it would cost $19 million to obtain the additional trains and $10 million in additional operating costs to expand into weekend services, and increase the number of daily rides from 34 to 40.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For five weeknights in November 2018, Sunrail is going to run late trains for guests attending sports events at the Arena. The last trains of the night will depart at 10:30 PM; one  heading to the northern end of the route, and one heading to the southern end of the route. Some test nights may not include the southern train.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fare_system_and_ticketing">Fare system and ticketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Fare system and ticketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Riders on the SunRail system use a <a href="/wiki/Stored-value_card" title="Stored-value card">stored-value card</a>, in the form of a disposable ticket or a reloadable SunCard, to pay fares. The cost of SunRail tickets is based on the number of counties (zones) through which the rider will be travelling. The system passes through four counties: <a href="/wiki/Volusia_County,_Florida" title="Volusia County, Florida">Volusia</a>; <a href="/wiki/Seminole_County,_Florida" title="Seminole County, Florida">Seminole</a>; <a href="/wiki/Orange_County,_Florida" title="Orange County, Florida">Orange</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Osceola_County,_Florida" title="Osceola County, Florida">Osceola</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sunrail.com_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sunrail.com-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> SunRail uses a "tap on/tap off" system for ticketing. Riders must "tap on" at a validator unit at the station prior to boarding the train by tapping their ticket on the screen and waiting for the beep. Riders must again "tap off" at a validator unit with their ticket after disembarking at their destination before exiting the station. Reduced fares are available for seniors, students, and disabled riders.<sup id="cite_ref-sunrailfares_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sunrailfares-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Plans for a mobile ticketing app were announced in May 2019. Development was expected to cost $200,000.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Technical">Technical</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Technical">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sunrail-MP32PH-Q.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Sunrail-MP32PH-Q.jpg/220px-Sunrail-MP32PH-Q.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Sunrail-MP32PH-Q.jpg/330px-Sunrail-MP32PH-Q.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Sunrail-MP32PH-Q.jpg/440px-Sunrail-MP32PH-Q.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sunrail-MP32PH-Q.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An <a href="/wiki/MPI_MPXpress" title="MPI MPXpress">MPI MP32PH-Q</a> locomotive in SunRail livery in September 2013.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations_and_maintenance">Operations and maintenance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Operations and maintenance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In addition to SunRail commuter trains, the line is used by three daily round trip <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> trains (the <a href="/wiki/Silver_Meteor" title="Silver Meteor">Silver Meteor</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Silver_Star_(Amtrak_train)" title="Silver Star (Amtrak train)">Silver Star</a> and <a href="/wiki/Auto_Train" title="Auto Train">Auto Train</a>), as well as by a handful of CSX freight trains. SunRail connects directly with the <i>Silver Star</i> and <i>Silver Meteor</i> in Winter Park, Orlando and Kissimmee, and the Sanford SunRail station is a five-minute drive from the <a href="/wiki/Sanford_station_(Amtrak)" title="Sanford station (Amtrak)">Sanford Auto Train station</a>. Phase 2 will offer a fourth connection at DeLand.
</p><p>The line was also used by Amtrak's tri-weekly <a href="/wiki/Sunset_Limited" title="Sunset Limited">Sunset Limited</a> which ran between Orlando and Los Angeles. However, service has been suspended indefinitely between Orlando and New Orleans since 2005 due to damage caused to the line by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a>.
</p><p>The Florida Department of Transportation announced on April 16, 2013, that it had awarded <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Transportation" title="Bombardier Transportation">Bombardier Technology</a> a $195 million contract to provide operation and maintenance services for SunRail, which includes train operations, dispatching, track and equipment maintenance, customer service, station platform &amp; facility maintenance, and materials supply. Bombardier assumed the operations and maintenance responsibilities in the spring of 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Progressive_Railroading_04/16/2013_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Progressive_Railroading_04/16/2013-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On Monday, July 29, 2013, at 3:30 AM, the Florida Department of Transportation assumed all train dispatching duties along the SunRail corridor from CSX. This event officially marked the end of CSX's involvement with the operations of the line, transferring total operational control of the corridor to the state of Florida. Since the hand off from CSX, all train dispatching has been handled by the CFRC Dispatcher out of the Operations Control Center at Rand Yard in Sanford, Florida.
</p><p>Operational testing of the SunRail equipment began on October 26, 2013, along the corridor between the DeBary and Maitland stations. The test train, which consisted of a locomotive and two cab cars, was part of a 2,500 mile "burn-in" period that is required prior to the start of revenue service. Over 100 similar test runs took place over the following months to ensure that the new trains, wayside signals and grade crossing signals operated correctly, as well as to verify that the trains properly aligned with each station platform.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On Friday, January 31, 2014, the Florida Department of Transportation announced that SunRail would begin service on May 1, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> SunRail initially offered a series of free test runs in April,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> but canceled them and instead decided to open for free for the first two weeks of service in May. This enabled remaining work to be completed in time. SunRail warned passengers who already purchased fare cards not to use their fare cards during the free run, or they may be deducted fares.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The SunRail grand opening was held at the Sand Lake Station at 11:00am EDT on Wednesday, April 30, 2014. This was preceded by a series of openings at the other stations, starting at the DeBary Station at 8:15am EDT, and progressing south down the line through the other stations at 15-minute intervals.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Passenger operations officially commenced on Thursday, May 1, 2014, with the first revenue service train departing south out of the Sanford Station at 5:06am EDT.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Sunrail trains operate at speeds between 30 and 79 miles per hour (48 and 127&#160;km/h), with an average speed of 33 miles per hour (53&#160;km/h), including stops.<sup id="cite_ref-os20140521_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-os20140521-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>All SunRail operations and maintenance personnel are employees of Bombardier Transportation. Approximately 24 engineers and conductors are on the operating roster at any given time. SunRail train crews (engineers &amp; conductors) are represented by the <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_Sheet_Metal,_Air,_Rail_and_Transportation_Workers" title="International Association of Sheet Metal, Air, Rail and Transportation Workers">International Association of Sheet Metal, Air, Rail and Transportation Workers</a> labor union (formerly known as the United Transportation Union (UTU).)
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rolling_stock">Rolling stock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Rolling stock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Sunrail trains operate at speeds between 30 and 79 miles per hour (48 and 127&#160;km/h), with an average speed of 33 miles per hour (53&#160;km/h), including stops.<sup id="cite_ref-os20140521_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-os20140521-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Each car is fully wheelchair accessible and equipped with a restroom, space for bicycles, electrical outlets for laptops and phone chargers, and free <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-experience_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-experience-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> In 2011 the Florida Department of Transportation ordered fourteen <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_BiLevel_Coach" title="Bombardier BiLevel Coach">BiLevel coaches</a> from <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Transportation" title="Bombardier Transportation">Bombardier Transportation</a> for $41 million, with an option for 46 additional cars.<sup id="cite_ref-bilevel_order_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bilevel_order-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> This order was later expanded to twenty, with the first cars arriving in Florida on July 20, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-obj20130731_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obj20130731-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MotivePower_Industries" class="mw-redirect" title="MotivePower Industries">MotivePower Industries</a> supplied eleven <a href="/wiki/MPI_MP32PH-Q" class="mw-redirect" title="MPI MP32PH-Q">MPI MP32PH-Q</a> <a href="/wiki/Diesel_locomotives" class="mw-redirect" title="Diesel locomotives">diesel locomotives</a>, rebuilt from former <a href="/wiki/Morrison-Knudsen" class="mw-redirect" title="Morrison-Knudsen">Morrison-Knudsen</a> <a href="/wiki/GP40WH-2" class="mw-redirect" title="GP40WH-2">GP40WH-2</a> locomotives which previously operated on MARC. These were ordered on September 12, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Trains_Magazine_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trains_Magazine-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The first locomotive, #100, arrived on October 1, 2013 via <a href="/wiki/CSX_Transportation" title="CSX Transportation">CSX</a> freight train at the SunRail Operations Control Center in Sanford, Florida, from the MotivePower plant in Boise, Idaho. In December 2017, the eleventh Locomotive was delivered, carrying Road Number 110<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Paint_scheme">Paint scheme</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Paint scheme">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On September 10, 2010, the Central Florida Commuter Rail Commission chose a paint scheme for the trains.<sup id="cite_ref-paint_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paint-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The design featured a sun along with renderings of green for wildlife and blue for skies.<sup id="cite_ref-paint_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paint-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> According to the designer, Jim Bockstall, the scheme was based on public input and was intended to include both movement and traditional imagery.<sup id="cite_ref-paint_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-paint-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety_and_security">Safety and security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Safety and security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Florida_Health_SunRail_Station;_North_Pedestrian_Xing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Florida_Health_SunRail_Station%3B_North_Pedestrian_Xing.jpg/220px-Florida_Health_SunRail_Station%3B_North_Pedestrian_Xing.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Florida_Health_SunRail_Station%3B_North_Pedestrian_Xing.jpg/330px-Florida_Health_SunRail_Station%3B_North_Pedestrian_Xing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Florida_Health_SunRail_Station%3B_North_Pedestrian_Xing.jpg/440px-Florida_Health_SunRail_Station%3B_North_Pedestrian_Xing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Florida_Health_SunRail_Station;_North_Pedestrian_Xing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Safety features at stations include bells, gates, and LED displays</div></div></div>
<p>In the months leading up to SunRail going operational, the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Department_of_Transportation" title="Florida Department of Transportation">Florida Department of Transportation</a> (FDOT) ran an aggressive public-safety campaign to warn drivers and passengers about railroad safety<sup id="cite_ref-os20140522_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-os20140522-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> using pamphlets, puppet shows for children, <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and even a Safety Mascot Squirrel named Tie.<sup id="cite_ref-bn9-20130907_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn9-20130907-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>  Despite this effort, SunRail has experienced several accidents with both motorists and pedestrians. Nearly a year into service, officials began installing dial-up grade crossing systems at grade crossings that are located closest to the stations. This system allows train crews to manually activate grade crossing warning devices (i.e. crossing gates, lights and bells) from the locomotive cab via key-coded radio transmission, thus eliminating the confusion of the grade crossing warning devices automatically activating, deactivating and reactivating whenever trains approach, stop at and depart the stations.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Security on the train and at stations is the responsibility of FDOT.  The FDOT does not employ a security force and relies solely on surveillance cameras and emergency call boxes.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Uniformed police officers are permitted to ride SunRail free of charge.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Grade_crossing_accidents">Grade crossing accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Grade crossing accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Because of the flat terrain and high water table of the Orlando area, the entire route of SunRail is at grade. Most road crossings except for expressways are not grade-separated; even major arterials like Route <a href="/wiki/US_Route_17" class="mw-redirect" title="US Route 17">17</a>/<a href="/wiki/US_Route_92" class="mw-redirect" title="US Route 92">92</a> have level crossings in populated areas. There are 96 grade crossings along the Phase 1 route, with an additional 30 on Phase 2.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> SunRail dramatically increased frequencies on the line, with 34 daily trips. Six daily Amtrak trains (three round trips) continue to operate, while 20 daily freights have largely been moved to the CSX "S" Line to the west.<sup id="cite_ref-prone_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prone-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Within the first five months of regular operations, SunRail trains were involved in four grade crossing accidents, all caused by driver error. <a href="/wiki/Florida_Highway_Patrol" title="Florida Highway Patrol">Florida Highway Patrol</a> officials blamed the crashes on drivers who were too impatient to wait for trains to pass and did not understand that trains cannot stop quickly.<sup id="cite_ref-prone_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prone-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tri-Rail" title="Tri-Rail">Tri-Rail</a>, which operates in a very similar densely populated area with many grade crossings, had 93 crashes during its first 15 years, though other systems saw their rates decrease after the initial months.<sup id="cite_ref-prone_79-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prone-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> After two more driver-caused accidents in early 2013, police increased enforcement of drivers bypassing crossing gates in an attempt to prevent additional crashes.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to an accident on October 8, 2015, where a dump truck was parked too close to the tracks and was side-swiped by a train, the Florida Highway Patrol has begun monitoring crossings and station areas. Billboards and mailers about train safety will also be put out to raise awareness. <sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Positive_train_control_technology">Positive train control technology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Positive train control technology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>With the southern extension nearing completion, Sunrail has begun installing positive train control technology. This system keeps trains alerted to other trains ahead to prevent collisions. This system was mandated by the government. The deadline was for the end of 2018, but if Sunrail meets certain criteria they can extend the deadline for full implementation to 2020. Wabtec, a Wilmerding, Pennsylvania, company, was awarded a $62 million contract to design, install, test, and implement the safety technology. SunRail Executive Director Nicola Liquori believes full implementation on the 61-mile system will be in place by December 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plans_and_expansions">Plans and expansions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Plans and expansions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>SunRail divided their startup operations into two phases. Phase 1 opened on May 1, 2014, between DeBary and Sand Lake Road. Due to budgetary constrains, Phase 2 was further divided in two separate segments; the completed <i>Phase 2 South</i> and uncompleted <i>Phase 2 North</i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Phase_2_North">Phase 2 North</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Phase 2 North">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DeBary_SunRail_Station;_Northbound_Dead_End_Bumper.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/DeBary_SunRail_Station%3B_Northbound_Dead_End_Bumper.JPG/220px-DeBary_SunRail_Station%3B_Northbound_Dead_End_Bumper.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/DeBary_SunRail_Station%3B_Northbound_Dead_End_Bumper.JPG/330px-DeBary_SunRail_Station%3B_Northbound_Dead_End_Bumper.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/DeBary_SunRail_Station%3B_Northbound_Dead_End_Bumper.JPG/440px-DeBary_SunRail_Station%3B_Northbound_Dead_End_Bumper.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DeBary_SunRail_Station;_Northbound_Dead_End_Bumper.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Looking north from the DeBary station; SunRail plans to expand north to DeLand from here</div></div></div>
<p><i>Phase 2 North</i> plans to extend the system 13 miles north from DeBary to the existing <a href="/wiki/DeLand_station" title="DeLand station">DeLand Amtrak station</a>.  
</p><p>However, on October 29, 2015, SunRail officials were denied a $35 million federal grant for the 13 mile <i>Phase 2 North</i> extension to Deland in Volusia County due to low ridership projections. County and SunRail officials were counting on this money to help pay for half of the $70 million cost to build this extension.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> In wake of not receiving federal funding, an additional station in <a href="/wiki/Orange_City,_Florida" title="Orange City, Florida">Orange City</a> is now being considered to boost ridership projections along the <i>Phase 2 North</i> extension.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Florida Department of Transportation said on May 3, 2016, that the northern extension of SunRail to DeLand has been halted due to the inability to obtain the necessary funds. The cost of this extension is estimated at $77 million, with half paid by grants and the other half by the FDOT. They have said they will continue to look for funding for the Phase 2 northern extension. <sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Phase_3_.28Orlando_International_Airport_connection.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Phase_3_(Orlando_International_Airport_connection)">Phase 3 (Orlando International Airport connection)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Phase 3 (Orlando International Airport connection)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>SunRail officials in the mid-2010s began investigating a Phase 3 expansion, which would include a connection to <a href="/wiki/Orlando_International_Airport" title="Orlando International Airport">Orlando International Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-articles.orlandosentinel.com_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-articles.orlandosentinel.com-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Currently this connection requires transferring to a shuttle bus at <a href="/wiki/Sand_Lake_Road_(SunRail_station)" class="mw-redirect" title="Sand Lake Road (SunRail station)">Sand Lake Road Station</a>.  The 5.5 mile route under consideration would travel 3.5 miles along an existing <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Utilities_Commission" title="Orlando Utilities Commission">Orlando Utilities Commission (OUC)</a> rail spur, which runs along the southern boundary of the airport's property and is used exclusively by coal trains to serve the Curtis H. Stanton Energy Center in eastern Orange County.  From there, two options were considered; one plan would have SunRail trains branch north off of the existing OUC line and onto a new 2-mile spur that would terminate at the planned South Airport Intermodal Terminal. The second option explored would be to build a transfer station along the OUC line where passengers would transfer from SunRail trains onto <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> trains that would run along a dedicated 2-mile line between the transfer and airport stations.<sup id="cite_ref-articles.orlandosentinel.com_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-articles.orlandosentinel.com-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Once at the South Airport Intermodal Terminal, passengers would transfer onto an <a href="/wiki/People_mover" title="People mover">Automated People Mover (APM)</a> that would take them the 1.5 mile distance north to the existing airport terminal. Passengers would also be able to transfer directly to <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Trains_USA" title="Virgin Trains USA">Virgin Trains USA</a> trains, a privately funded <a href="/wiki/Inter-city_rail" title="Inter-city rail">Inter-city rail</a> passenger service of the <a href="/wiki/Florida_East_Coast_Railway" title="Florida East Coast Railway">Florida East Coast Railway</a>, currently under development, which would offer sixteen daily roundtrips to <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> starting in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-articles.orlandosentinel.com_86-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-articles.orlandosentinel.com-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Direct transfers would also be available to one of two proposed alternatives; either a <a href="/wiki/Orlando_maglev" title="Orlando maglev">Maglev train</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> train, both of which are planned to run between the South Airport Intermodal Terminal and <a href="/wiki/International_Drive" title="International Drive">International Drive</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The cost of the Phase 3 expansion was originally estimated at $100 million.<sup id="cite_ref-4/17_sentinel_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4/17_sentinel-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2015, SunRail officials submitted a request to the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Transit_Administration" title="Federal Transit Administration">Federal Transit Administration (FTA)</a> to move the project from the initial planning phase into the project development phase, which it approved on October 26, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>  In April 2017, a state study of constructing trackage to the airport found that it would cost about $250 million, and with no funding sources identified the project was left with no timetable for execution.<sup id="cite_ref-4/17_sentinel_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4/17_sentinel-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Daytona_Beach_extension">Daytona Beach extension</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Daytona Beach extension">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On April 17, 2014, <a href="/wiki/Volusia_County,_Florida" title="Volusia County, Florida">Volusia County</a> and FDOT funded a $2.5 million study to investigate the cost, preliminary design and ridership of a SunRail extension to <a href="/wiki/Daytona_Beach,_Florida" title="Daytona Beach, Florida">Daytona Beach</a>.  As part of this effort, Volusia County wants to see the <a href="/wiki/Interstate_4" title="Interstate 4">Interstate 4</a> median width maintained as a possible future rail corridor.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lakeland_extension">Lakeland extension</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Lakeland extension">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The 2035 Polk County Mobility Vision Plan envisions extending SunRail into Polk County, with stations at Haines City, Auburndale, and Lakeland. Each station would be built in separate phases.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sanford_Airport_extension">Sanford Airport extension</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=SunRail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Sanford Airport extension">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Seminole County officials have brought up the possibility of extending SunRail to <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Sanford_International_Airport" title="Orlando Sanford International Airport">Orlando Sanford International Airport</a> via an existing 4-mile freight spur. The Florida Department of Transportation has a contractual option to lease the spur from CSX for 30 years after 2007 for $10.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.orlandosentinel.com/news/sunrail/os-sunrail-fares-low-20150510-story.html">"SunRail finishes first year $27.2 million in the red"</a>. <i>Orlando Sentinel</i>. 10 May 2015<span class="reference-accessdate">.
